## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of position x) and possibly damping forces (functions of velocity v). Classical nonlinear oscillators include Duffing, Van der Pol, and other variants with polynomial or transcendental nonlinearities in x and v.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping with restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v (position-velocity coupling nonlinearity)
- Driven oscillator (periodic): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven with sinusoidal forcing)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinear restoring and damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force as in a pendulum)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity with linear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential well / symmetric oscillation about equilibrium
- Even-power restoring terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential, broken symmetry in oscillation
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v → linear energy dissipation or injection (positive/negative damping)
- Position-dependent damping coefficient (e.g., (1 - x**2)*v) → self-sustained limit-cycle oscillations (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(c*x) → large-amplitude pendulum-like dynamics with non-polynomial restoring force
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system; presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → forced/driven oscillator
- Product terms x*v or x**2*v → parametric coupling between position and velocity indicating energy exchange nonlinearity
- Cubic position term with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x**3) → double-well (Duffing) or softening/hardening spring behavior

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.19483*v + 0.19483*v*x**2 - 3.04924*x*exp(-|x|) - 0.14305*sin(v)`

Key features of GT:
1. Linear term in `v`
2. `v*x**2` term
3. `x*exp(-|x|)` term - this is crucial and distinctive
4. `sin(v)` term - depends on `v`, not `x`

The `x*exp(-|x|)` term is NOT a polynomial, NOT a simple exponential, and NOT expressible as `sin(x)` or polynomial combinations. It has a kink at x=0 due to |x|.

The `sin(v)` term depends on `v`, which is fundamentally different from `sin(x)`.

Let me now check each candidate systematically. Most candidates have `sin(c*x)` instead of `sin(v)`, and polynomial/trigonometric terms in `x` instead of `x*exp(-|x|)`. I'll focus on candidates that could potentially match.

**Key observations for quick elimination:**
- Any candidate without `sin(v)` (or equivalent) cannot match, since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from functions of `x` and `v` alone.
- Any candidate without `x*exp(-|x|)` (or equivalent) cannot match, since `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by polynomials or `sin(x)` terms.

Let me check if any candidate has both `sin(v)` and `x*exp(-|x|)`:

Going through all candidates: None of them contain `sin(v)` - they all have `sin(c*x)` or similar functions of `x`. The GT requires `sin(v)`, which is a fundamentally different basis function that cannot be produced by any function of `x` alone.

Additionally, the `x*exp(-|x|)` term requires `exp(-|x|)`, and `|x|` appears in none of the candidates. Some candidates have `exp(c*x)` or `exp(c*x**2)`, but `exp(c*x)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)` for all x (since |x| ≠ -x for positive x), and `exp(c*x**2)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)`.

Let me verify: Could `sin(v)` be approximated by `c*v` for small v? No - the rules explicitly forbid asymptotic approximations. They must be EXACTLY equal.

Since NO candidate contains `sin(v)` as a basis function, and `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all other basis functions present (polynomials in x, v, sin(x), exp(x), etc.), no candidate can match the GT.

For completeness, let me also note that `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be exactly represented by any finite polynomial, `sin(x)` combination, or `exp(cx)` or `exp(cx²)` terms.
